## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv/dt) is determined by nonlinear restoring forces in position x, possibly nonlinear damping in velocity v, and potentially time-dependent driving forces. The governing equation is Newton's second law with nonlinear force terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (mixed damping model)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (canonical chaotic oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x²) in restoring force → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²*v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillations (van der Pol type)
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) → Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation distinguishing small vs large amplitude behavior
- Trigonometric functions of time (sin/cos of c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Product of position powers with velocity (x^n * v) → energy-dependent damping where dissipation varies with oscillation amplitude
- Negative linear damping combined with positive nonlinear damping (c1*v + c2*v³ with opposite signs) → limit cycle behavior
- Rational functions of position x/(1+c*x²) → bounded restoring force modeling saturation of spring stiffness
